    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText2585414661773713392" style="display:none"><b>He was everything she'd sworn to avoid.</b><br /><br />Poppy Hathaway loves her unconventional family, though she longs for normalcy. Then fate leads to a meeting with Harry Rutledge, an enigmatic hotel owner and inventor with wealth, power, and a dangerous hidden life. When their flirtation compromises her own reputation, Poppy shocks everyone by accepting his proposal—only to find that her new husband offers his passion, but not his trust.<br /><br /><b>And she was everything he needed.</b><br /><br />Harry was willing to do anything to win Poppy—except to open his heart. All his life, he has held the world at arm’s length…but the sharp, beguiling Poppy demands to be his wife in <i>every</i> way that matters. Still, as desire grows between them, an enemy lurks in the shadows. Now if Harry wants to keep Poppy by his side, he must forge a true union of body and soul, once and for all...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766627361?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766627361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3227450476158490218"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392393570i/8550925.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let’s make one thing clear; this book is an HR duck. It looks like one, it talks like one, and it walks like one. Is it formulaic? Probably. Should I have enjoyed it as much as I did? Probably not. Am I giving it five stars anyway? Absolutely. Why? <br/><br/>Because fuck you, that’s why. <br/><br/>I should start posting disclaimers at the top of my reviews for HRs stating that my opinion probably shouldn’t be trusted. <br/><br/>For those of you who know me, you know how many literary pet peeves I have. For those of you who d</span>
  <span id="freeText3227450476158490218" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392393570i/8550925.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let’s make one thing clear; this book is an HR duck. It looks like one, it talks like one, and it walks like one. Is it formulaic? Probably. Should I have enjoyed it as much as I did? Probably not. Am I giving it five stars anyway? Absolutely. Why? <br><br>Because fuck you, that’s why. <br><br>I should start posting disclaimers at the top of my reviews for HRs stating that my opinion probably shouldn’t be trusted. <br><br>For those of you who know me, you know how many literary pet peeves I have. For those of you who don’t know me, I have a lot of literary pet peeves. Too many of them in one book and I’ll start docking stars. <br><br><b>EXCEPT FOR IN HISTORICAL ROMANCES.</b><br><br>I’m a little embarrassed to say that I actually…look forward to overused themes and tropes in HRs. If they’re not present, I’m usually disappointed. Most of the time they don’t even have to be well written and I’ll still enjoy the hell out of them. What can I say? It’s my guilty pleasure genre. <br><br>Well, this book IS well written. It’s also well researched. I’m a history geek so I’m always happy when an author sneaks in some real facts about the time period and setting. Kleypas included quite a few without overcomplicating the story. <br><br>The plot is a popular one in this genre. The female lead, Poppy, gets trapped into marrying the devilish Harry Rutledge after being caught in a compromising position with him. <br><br>Other well executed tropes include the “I’m so damaged, no one will love me” male lead, the Mary Sue female lead who’s different than her peers because she’s intelligent and not afraid to own it, the meddling family, the silly misunderstandings, the witty banter, the HEA, the list goes on and on. <br><br>And you know what? I enjoyed every damn minute of it. If you’re a Historical Romance fangirl, you should give this a try. Or if you’re just in the mood for something fun and entertaining, you should do the same.<br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3227450476158490218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Tempt Me at Twilight, (stand-alone). The wicked, ruthless & unforgettable Harry Rutledge sets his sights on Poppy Hathaway!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it’s possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.”</b>

</a><br/><u>Books in Hathaways series are stand-alone, but most enjoyed if read in order:</u><br/><b>Book 1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389865' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mine Till Midnight</a><br/>Book 2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485390077' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seduce Me at Sunrise</a><br/>Book 3: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389969' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tempt Me at Twilight</a><br/>Book 4: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485390188' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Married By </a></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5121930043795373002" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514003532i/24742026._SX540_.jpg" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513753475ra/24718147.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513753818ra/24718167.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513753818ra/24718168.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513753818ra/24718169.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️! Tempt Me at Twilight, (stand-alone). The wicked, ruthless &amp; unforgettable Harry Rutledge sets his sights on Poppy Hathaway!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it’s possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><u>Books in Hathaways series are stand-alone, but most enjoyed if read in order:</u><br><b>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389865" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485390077" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Seduce Me at Sunrise</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389969" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tempt Me at Twilight</a><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485390188" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Married By Morning</a><br>Book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485390334" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Love in the Afternoon</a></b><br><br><b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> (stand-alone) opens up to <b>Poppy Hathaway</b> spending her third season in London in hopes of <b>catching a husband.</b> Her unconventional upbringing, scholarly personality and desire for a dull husband has complicated matters. But finally, she has a suitor lined up until an <b>mysterious stranger</b> rattles and intrigues her in equal measures.<br><br>A chance encounter with hotelier, inventor and business man <b>Harry Rutledge</b> will change everything. <br><br>Harry has never met a problem he couldn’t solve, opportunity he couldn’t capitalize on nor a woman he couldn’t bed. <b>What Harry wants he gets</b> and he has set his sights on Poppy. The story goes on to follow them as Poppy is pulled into Harry’s <b>game of scandal and seduction.</b> But before long lines are blurred and crossed until it’s no longer clear who is the seducer or seduced. Let’s hope they can both escape with their hearts intact.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“The third time, I’m going to do things that will mortify you when you remember them tomorrow.” He kissed her gently. “And you’ll love that most of all.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514003532ra/24742027.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nine words to describe <b>(Jay) Harry Rutledge:</b> possessive, devious, determined, mysterious, broken, aloof, selfish, blunt and ruthless.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“She was yours, if you’d truly wanted her,” Harry continued, a pitiless smile touching his lips. “But I wanted her more.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514003532ra/24742028.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven words to describe <b>Poppy Hathaway:</b> smart, outspoken, charismatic, naïve, good-natured, insightful and trusting.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You have experience with hedgehogs?” <br>“No.” He slanted a smile at her. “But I have some experience with prickly females.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>Tempt Me at Twilight,</b> told from multiple POVs in third person, is <b>butterflies-in-your belly romance</b> at its best; sexy, funny, suspenseful with a pinch of angst. I'm happy to report it is just as good this time around - one of the best historicals I have read with Harry Rutledge as and all-time favorite hero.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Trying to understand Harry Rutledge was like taking apart one of the intricate clockwork mechanisms he had constructed. One could examine every gear and ratchet wheel and lever, but that didn’t mean one would ever comprehend what made it all work.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_49168772" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49168772" />
    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1918270-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460302951p2/1918270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49168772?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=dik">dik</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=to-blog">to-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49168772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8667220719286472524">What can I say? I just love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas' title='Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lisa Kleypas</a>'s writing and, as far as I know, she can do no wrong. Okay, I haven't read <i>all</i> her backlist yet, but almost everything I've read so far was excellent. The only exception was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_' title='Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mine Till Midnight</a>, but even so it was good enough and definitely worth reading.<br/><br/>Poppy Hathaway is in London for her third season and, as it has become usual, she's staying with her family at the Rutledge Hotel. As the story opens, she's chasing her sister Beatrix's ferret, trying to r</span>
  <span id="freeText8667220719286472524" style="display:none">What can I say? I just love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas" title="Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Kleypas</a>'s writing and, as far as I know, she can do no wrong. Okay, I haven't read <i>all</i> her backlist yet, but almost everything I've read so far was excellent. The only exception was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_" title="Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a>, but even so it was good enough and definitely worth reading.<br /><br />Poppy Hathaway is in London for her third season and, as it has become usual, she's staying with her family at the Rutledge Hotel. As the story opens, she's chasing her sister Beatrix's ferret, trying to recover a love letter the mischievous animal has stolen from her. The last thing Poppy needs is to have the love letter she's received from her secret beau, the Hon. Michael Bayning, falling in anyone else's hands and becoming public, so she has no qualms leaving her private room unescorted and following the darn ferret through the hotel. On her merry chase, she ends up meeting the reclusive and mysterious Harry Rutledge, the hotel owner, and the course of her entire life is changed.<br /><br />Harry is a very successful self-made man who always gets what he wants, no matter what. And the moment he meets Poppy, he decides he wants her. So he sets out to get her. Thanks to some luck and some ruthless machinations of his part, he doesn't waste any time taking her secret beau out of the picture and planting himself firmly on his place. Poppy is hurt in the process, but that was bound to happen eventually even without his interference, so Harry is convinced it's all for the best.<br /><br />In a short time, Harry gets what he wants - that is, Poppy - and they get married against her family's objections. At this point, Harry's part in ruining Poppy's relationship with Michael is known to all the Hathaways - Poppy included - so they neither like or trust him. But Poppy goes along with marrying him anyway, basically choosing the lesser of two evils. Harry's determined to win his wife's affection - not her love, because he doesn't know what that is - while Poppy's decided to keep her distance. Well, we all know how this ends, because there's no resisting a Kleypas hero. ;)<br /><br />The Hathaways are an "eccentric" family, to say the least, and Poppy has always been the "odd one out" to me because she doesn't embrace her family's quirkiness and craves a "normal" and sedate life. That doesn't mean she's estranged from them or that she's ashamed of them, but she dreams of a different life for herself. That's why I fully understood her infatuation with Michael, the son of a viscount and the epitome of everything proper and traditional. And that's why I cut her some slack for taking so long to let him go from her heart and <i>accept</i> Harry.<br /><br />Notice that I used the word "accept" and not "forgive", because I really don't think there was anything to be forgiven there. Harry didn't lie, although he didn't always reveal everything he knew, and he didn't force Poppy to kiss him to compromise her. On the contrary, she was fully enjoying his kisses even though she thought she was in love with another man! Okay, Harry was ruthless and manipulative (but not cruel), went after what he wanted with determination and took advantage of the situation, but he didn't make anything up. He only accelerated the process, so to speak, because that weakling Michael would never be brave enough to go against his father. Poppy deserved someone who loved her above everything else, and that man was Harry. I simply <i>adored</i> Harry! He's way up there in the altar of my favorite heroes, along with Sebastian, Lord St. Vincent (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>) and Derek Craven (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/330721.Dreaming_of_You__Gamblers___2_" title="Dreaming of You (Gamblers, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreaming of You</a>). Not by coincidence, all 3 of them are perfect examples of how <i>good</i> a "bad boy" can be when he finds the right woman... Hmmm, do I see a pattern in my "obsession"? ;)<br /><br />As in all the previous books in the <b>Hathaways</b> series, there were a lot of scenes that weren't solely focused on the H/h's interactions. That bothered me when I read the 1st book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_" title="Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a>, but now I think they're part of this series' charm and those "secondary scenes" add depth to the story. In this particular book, I got to know and understand Harry much better by learning how his employees saw him and that was a plus. I also got to know something very interesting about Ms. Marks, Poppy and Beatrix's former governess and current companion and chaperone, and I can't wait to see her bring Leo to heel.<br /><br />And last but not least, the now (in)famous cliffhanger... I loved it! I know a lot of readers were annoyed by it, but I thought it was delicious. I'm not ashamed to say, I closed the book with a sigh and a a smile.<br /><br />Great story, to-die-for hero, lovable heroine, witty dialogue, steamy love scenes, funny and charming secondary characters... This was an excellent read.<br /><br />And just because I love quotes, I'm going to finish my review with one of my favorite passages in the book:<br /><br /><i>"I want you any way I can get you. Not because you’re beautiful or clever or kind or adorable, although the devil knows you’re all those things. I want you because there’s no one else like you, and I don’t ever want to start a day without seeing you."<br /><br />As Poppy opened her mouth to reply, he smoothed his thumb across her lower lip, coaxing her to wait until he had finished. "Do you know what a balance wheel is?"<br /><br />She shook her head slightly.<br /><br />"There’s one in every clock or watch. It rotates back and forth without stopping. It’s what makes the ticking sound... what makes the hands move forward to mark the minutes. Without it, the watch wouldn’t work. You’re my balance wheel, Poppy."</i><br /><br />Call me crazy, but I thought that was one of the most romantic declarations of love I've read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8667220719286472524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83121200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83121200" />
    <a title="Auntee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886675-auntee"><img alt="Auntee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281897695p2/886675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83121200?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntee" href="/user/show/886675-auntee">Auntee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Historical romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=lisa-kleypas">lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=2010_reads">2010_reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83121200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer985565159206941736">Ahhh....I don't even feel like writing a review for this one except to say "Move over Cam, and make room for Harry!" <br/><br/>I found out something about myself--I love a romance where the hero really <i>needs</i> for someone to love him, whether he realizes it or not. And handsome hotelier Harry Rutledge (early 30s), who both wanted and feared affection (due to a heartbreaking childhood)--he captured my heart. Yes, he started out as a manipulative, selfish devil, (the way he got Poppy (23) to marry him), but h</span>
  <span id="freeText985565159206941736" style="display:none">Ahhh....I don't even feel like writing a review for this one except to say "Move over Cam, and make room for Harry!" <br><br>I found out something about myself--I love a romance where the hero really <i>needs</i> for someone to love him, whether he realizes it or not. And handsome hotelier Harry Rutledge (early 30s), who both wanted and feared affection (due to a heartbreaking childhood)--he captured my heart. Yes, he started out as a manipulative, selfish devil, (the way he got Poppy (23) to marry him), but how he ended up, while absorbing Poppy's love and affection...*sigh*. Enough said.<br><br>Here's some of my favorite scenes/quotes in this one:<br><br>*Dodger the ferret--so cute, so mischievous, so <i>smart</i>! Are ferrets really this smart, or is Dodger a mini-dog?:)<br><br>*This quote from Harry to Poppy about letting him court her, reminded me of a scene from <i>Gone With the Wind</i>, where Rhett speaks to Scarlett about marrying him...<br><br> <i>"You were courted by a boy, who had to do as he was told." His hot breath feathered against her lips as he whispered, "You should try it with a man, who needs no one's permission."</i><br><br>*Seeing all the Hathaways again, and seeing how Leo, Cam and Merripen were willing to physically do battle with Harry to protect Poppy. Love that family loyalty.<br><br>*When Cam told Harry that Poppy was "part of his tribe'. Yeah.<br><br>*When Harry's hotel staff, who loved Poppy, plotted to make sure that Harry and Poppy 'consumated' their marriage.<br><br>*That same hotel staff, discussing the state of the Rutledge's sex life:<br><br> <i>The chef looked deeply concerned. "You think there's a problem<br> with his carrot?"</i><br> "Alors, <i>he is a virile man...she is a beautiful woman...why <br> are they not making salad together?"</i><br><br>*When Poppy sprained her ankle and Harry used his influence to get special chocolates made for her. Aww...the beginnings of Harry allowing himself to care.<br><br>*Poppy and Leo's conversation about Harry's 'masculine problem': <br> <i>"Damn it. What exactly are we calling a 'masculine problem'? <br> Did he have trouble running the flag up? Or did it fall to <br> half-staff?"<br> "Do we have to speak of this metaphorically, or--"<br> "Yes," Leo said firmly.<br> "All right. He..."Poppy frowned in concentration as she<br> searched for the right words,"...left me while the flag was <br> still flying."</i><br><br>*The hotness that was Harry and Poppy together:<br> <i>I'm going to make love to you all night, Poppy. And the first time, you're going to feel very safe. But the second time, I'm going to be a little bit wicked...and you'll like that even more. And the third time---" he paused with a smile as he heard her breath catch. "The third time, I'm going to do things that will mortify you when you remember them tomorrow." He kissed her gently. "And you'll love that most of all."</i><br><br>Well there's plenty more where that came from, as well as plenty of chuckles, laugh-out-loud moments, wry humor (especially from Leo, who I've grown to appreciate), amusing moments with Beatrix and her menagerie, catching up with the whole Hathaway clan, and a tad bit of suspense near the end. Yet again, LK made it all fly by so fast. I've come to adore this quirky Hathaway family, and I'm in a bit of a panic knowing I only have two more stories to read. Lk reveals even more about Catherine Marks (Beatrix and Poppy's companion)--the mystery builds--what <i>did</i> happen to her? And you can see that Leo is finding himself more and more attracted to her....I can't wait to read their story!<br><br>This one wasn't as complicated, angsty, or dramatic as some of the other stories in the series, but I was still entertained. It must be that Kleypas magic that gets me to fall so easily for her characters. I was in dire need of reading a book that could 'take me away', and <i>Tempt Me At Twilight</i> certainly did that. Thank you, LK. 5 stars<br><br><br>My Harry...<br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=Tohr4.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380330249i/692351.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_55148431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55148431" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55148431?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lisa Kleypas fans, Historical romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=ruthless-hero">ruthless-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=nerd-prof-scientist-genius-geek">nerd-prof-scientist-genius-geek</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55148431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13989318177517701659">What can I say about this book? After reading the last pages of this novel, at approximately 1 am, I set it down, knowing I couldn't possibly be ready to write a coherent review. Reviews are like soups or dishes with tomatoes and hearty seasonings. They should sit and rest, letting the spices and the tomato paste mingle together, so that the flavor can be maximized. Accordingly, I let myself ruminate in a bovine fashion about what I would write in my review of the latest historical by one of my </span>
  <span id="freeText13989318177517701659" style="display:none">What can I say about this book? After reading the last pages of this novel, at approximately 1 am, I set it down, knowing I couldn't possibly be ready to write a coherent review. Reviews are like soups or dishes with tomatoes and hearty seasonings. They should sit and rest, letting the spices and the tomato paste mingle together, so that the flavor can be maximized. Accordingly, I let myself ruminate in a bovine fashion about what I would write in my review of the latest historical by one of my favorite authors, over the far too short weekend. <br /><br />First and foremost, Ms. Kleypas wrote yet another wonderful book that cements her place on my keeper and favorite author shelves. Secondly, she took a concept that I thought I was familiar with, but managed to surprise me, and keep me on my toes as I read. I thought I had this story all figured out, by some of the comments from my Goodreads friends, and in Amazon.com romance forum discussions, and my own preconceived notions based on the blurb, and what I know about how Ms. Kleypas writes books. But, I was still surprised.<br /><br />Harry Rutledge: This is a hero that is very hard to define. At times, frankly, I disliked him. I thought, he's not a nice man. He's very cold, and he's ruthless. But I loved him, at the same time, for being all the things I mentioned. He is definitely a standout for me because of the complexity of his nature. And I loved how Ms. Kleypas was unstinting in showing Harry in the worst light possible. She didn't go the heavy-handed route, in steering us into loving him because he was the hero of the story. And I respect her for that. In fact, I am glad for the naturalistic approach she adopted. Because, as I read this story, the man that Harry is, deep down, the man he wants to be, shows through. And for that, I have to give this author a high five. Harry is a carefully engineered survivor. What he went through in his childhood is not even close to the worst I have read about in fiction. However, for this <b> admitted </b> idealist who believes children should be loved and cherished, valued and tended carefully like the creations of beauty and worth that they are, it was pretty awful for a child to suffer that way. Harry grew up priviledged, but he was neglected in all the ways that count. If that wouldn't make a social maladroit out of a person, I'm not quite sure what would. But, at the same time, Harry managed to make something of himself. He didn't become a shiftless dilettante who did nothing but drinking, fornicating, and spend other people's money. He became a brilliant inventor, businessman, and empire-builder. Even a few of his enemies respected him enough to name their children after him. To be able to do that, I have to respect him. He was a monolith of admantine will, but so vulnerable in some ways, that few were privy to. In truth, only Poppy, that I could perceive, reading this story. <br /><br />When Harry Met Poppy: We all have defining moments in our lives. Harry had several. But the one that would change the course of his life irrevocably, was when he encountered Poppy. Ever wanted something so very much, the fierce desire for it burns like thirst in a parched throat? That's how Harry wanted Poppy. And that motivated him to do some very lousy things. In his mind, it was okay because Michael Beyning didn't deserve her. I think that he was right about the last part. Beyning didn't deserve a woman that he wouldn't fight for to all the heights and depths of his available resources. He barely even tried for her. And Harry's actions proved that. In medical terms, he performed an elective surgery that was more agressive than needed, but achieved results that no one could argue weren't successful. Yet, there were some significant side effects. For one, Poppy married him with the cold precision of a general going to war, and told him that she would never love him. Not the ideal way to start a marriage. Yet, in Harry's unfathomably analytical mind, he didn't care, because all he needed was her as his wife. The ends justified the means.<br /><br />What does a man do with a wife? What does a wife do with a husband that didn't fit her expectations of the husband she always wanted? Harry and Poppy had to learn these things. He couldn't put Poppy into a little cubbyhole to take out and amuse himself at his limited leisure. He couldn't wind her up like an automaton. Poppy was a living, breathing, force of nature, that would settle for no less than what she deserved. At times, Poppy came off as immature, in a sense. Hanging onto a fairy tale dream of marriage. But, I had to admire her for sticking to her guns about what she would and would not tolerate from her husband. She needed to do that, because Harry was very used to getting exactly what he wanted, by using the powerful force of his personality, and threats, if necessary. And Poppy did show that she could compromise and surrender in the ways that were important to make a marriage work. It's about meeting each other half-way, and they both had to learn to do that. I liked the dynamic between them, how they danced around each other, getting to know each other as husband and wife. Although the circumstances are purely out of romantic fiction, I think that aspect of marriage is very true to life. A young couple has unrealistic expectations of what they will experience in marriage, and the first year is a wakeup call, as they realize that real life isn't as cut and dried. Marriage takes compromise, time and energy, and lots of communication. You could see this being played out between Poppy and Harry. This is one deeper level that took me by surprise, although, knowing Ms. Kleypas, it probably shouldn't. She writes extremely romantic stories, but there is always some degree of realism in the intricacies of interpersonal relations that play out in her stories. I think she writes married stories very well, but then, she's been married for a long time, so she probably draws on the bank of that experience to develop such a rich narrative.<br /><br />Family, the Beauty of it: I realize that the Hathaway books aren't high on the list of some of Ms. Kleypas's fans. But, I love this series. It was like going to visit some friends in their family home, and seeing their family interactions, reading this book. So intensely familiar, and heart-warming. I was immersed in the love and the chaos that is the Hathaway family, which is ever-expanding. I got the opportunity to visit with some characters that I easily grew to love in prior books: Cam (he is such a show-stealer), Amelia (the mother hen), Beatrix (how adorable she is with her animals, and her sharply- perceptive understanding of human nature), Kev (intense and forthright, as always), Win (sweet, loving, and peaceful), Leo (who is really coming into his own, has a wonderful sense of humor, and a surprising strength of character that I love), and Catherine Marks (she is shaping up to be a very tortured character who has me very intrigued). <br /><br />Rounding up my thoughts: Tempt Me at Twilight turned out to be a very satisfying but hard to define read for me. There is something seemingly basic about it, compared to some of Kleypas's other books, but complicated at the same time. This book really is a book about marriage, and about letting the fairy tales go, and embracing the beauty in what is real, and accepting that your destiny doesn't come in the pretty packages that you shop for. Also realizing that the pretty possession that you wanted so bad, comes with a cost, and takes an emotional price in return. I feel that this book presents a deeper message about how your destiny comes exactly the way it's supposed to, although it may take growth on your part, and the partner that fate has decreed for you, to fully realize the potential that is there. As usual, Ms. Kleypas nails the Victorian period with the beauty of an Impressionist painting, not heavy, bold strokes, but with a light, careful, bright, and dreamy touch, that is all the more captivating to me as a reader. The end of this book marks the beginning of the next arc of this story. I am full of some reservations, and fears that my gentle heart is going to face some anguish ahead. I have questions and theories that have been brought to life by the conclusion of this story, if you can call it that. I suppose I will have to remember the adage to all readers of series: Keep Reading. I trust that I will be in for another delightful reading experience if I am able to do exactly that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13989318177517701659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-stalk-me-baby-possessive">hero-stalk-me-baby-possessive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=a-all-time-best-top-20-fave-dik">a-all-time-best-top-20-fave-dik</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=historical-romance-victorian">historical-romance-victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=best-secondary-characters-ensemble">best-secondary-characters-ensemble</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-broody-gruff-serious-moody">hero-broody-gruff-serious-moody</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57743711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12609379312064118099"><i>Re-read Oct'2019</i>:<br/><br/>I still loved it, but I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_' title='Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mine Till Midnight</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2948832.Seduce_Me_at_Sunrise__The_Hathaways___2_' title='Seduce Me at Sunrise (The Hathaways, #2) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seduce Me at Sunrise</a> better this time rereading the series. <i>The Hathaways</i> is absolutely one of my all-time favorite series! Still big 5+ stars! <br/><br/><i>Original read/review Jun'2010</i>:<br/><br/>5++ stars – Historical Romance<br/><br/><i>“Her chances of a decent marriage were about to be dashed-and all because of a ferret.”</i> And thus begins the wonderfully romantic third installment in the saga of the eccentric Hathaway family, <b>Tempt Me At Twilight</b>. <br/><br/>Poppy Hatha</span>
  <span id="freeText12609379312064118099" style="display:none"><i>Re-read Oct'2019</i>:<br /><br />I still loved it, but I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_" title="Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2948832.Seduce_Me_at_Sunrise__The_Hathaways___2_" title="Seduce Me at Sunrise (The Hathaways, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Seduce Me at Sunrise</a> better this time rereading the series. <i>The Hathaways</i> is absolutely one of my all-time favorite series! Still big 5+ stars! <br /><br /><i>Original read/review Jun'2010</i>:<br /><br />5++ stars – Historical Romance<br /><br /><i>“Her chances of a decent marriage were about to be dashed-and all because of a ferret.”</i> And thus begins the wonderfully romantic third installment in the saga of the eccentric Hathaway family, <b>Tempt Me At Twilight</b>. <br /><br />Poppy Hathaway loves her quirky family, but she yearns for a conventional, quiet, normal, stable, peaceful, predictable, albeit boring, life. She believes wholeheartedly that she’s found her true soul’s desire in her beloved Michael Bayning, who’s courted her in private but has so far withheld a proposal due to concerns over his father’s likely disapproval over the match. When fate (in the form of a wily, on the loose ferret named Dodger) results in a clandestine meeting with mysterious, wealthy, powerful, reclusive, hotelier Harry Rutledge, Poppy’s future is forever altered.<br /><br />Harry, owner of London’s most famous Rutledge Hotel, lives a rather solitary existence and never expects or desires to fall in love, but he’s immediately enamored and infatuated by lovely, intelligent, spirited Poppy and sets out to win her for himself. Poppy’s heart and devotion belong to Michael, but she still can’t help but be a bit intrigued and flattered by the enigmatic and dynamic Harry, especially with his persistent courtship and shocking proposal.<br /><br />When Poppy finds herself heartbroken and her reputation and future security at risk, she accepts Harry’s marriage proposal, but then painful secrets are revealed that shatter her trust and wound her aching heart even further. What does a woman do when she finds herself married to the villain?<br /><br />Kleypas is a master at turning tortured, cold, manipulative, cynical, ruthless men (even near villains) into the most sigh-delicious, swoon-worthy heroes in romance. Harry reminded me a little of Simon Hunt from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a>, only with a strong dose of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a> St. Vincent’s ruthlessness and vindictiveness thrown in. And sweet, caring, smart, bighearted, exuberant Poppy was the perfect compliment and match for cold-hearted, jaded, intrinsically lonely Harry...I just loved them together! <br /><br />Although I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_" title="Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a>, mainly for dreamy, yummy Cam Rohan, and loved Kev’s and Win’s achingly beautiful romance in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2948832.Seduce_Me_at_Sunrise__The_Hathaways___2_" title="Seduce Me at Sunrise (The Hathaways, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Seduce Me at Sunrise</a>, <b>Tempt Me At Twilight</b>, with its compelling, unforgettable story, beguiling, complex characters, strong depth of touching emotion, and lush sensuality that’s all blended together brilliantly, is vintage Kleypas and my favorite of the <i>Hathaways</i> series so far. It’s a splendid, moving, heartfelt, and utterly romantic read that’s completely riveting from beginning to end and just sheer historical romance perfection. Big 5 stars! <br /> <br />Here are some of my favorite moments/lines:<br /><br />***************Possible spoilers ahead***************<br /><br />Harry to Poppy:<br /><br /><i>“I’ll never be sorry about it. Because if I hadn’t done it, you’d be his now. And he only wanted you if it was easy for him. But I want you any way I can get you. Not because you’re beautiful or clever or kind or adorable, although devil knows you’re all those things. I want you because there’s no one else like you, and I don’t ever want to start a day without seeing you.”<br /><br />“Do you know what a balance wheel is?” She shook her head slightly. “There’s one in every clock or watch. It rotates back and forth without stopping. It’s what makes the ticking sound...what makes the hands move forward to mark the minutes. Without it, the watch wouldn’t work. You’re my balance wheel, Poppy.” <br /><br />“I have so much love for you, I could fill rooms with it. Buildings. You’re surrounded by it wherever you go, you walk through it, breathe it...it’s in your lungs, and under your tongue, and between your fingers and toes...” His mouth moved passionately over hers, urging her lips apart. It was a kiss to level mountains and shake stars from the sky. It was a kiss to make angels faint and demons weep...a passionate, demanding, soul-searing kiss that nearly knocked the earth off its axis. Or at least that was how Poppy felt about it.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12609379312064118099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_797535890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/797535890" />
    <a title="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19958389-christina-brunette-reader"><img alt="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532563583p2/19958389.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797535890?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" href="/user/show/19958389-christina-brunette-reader">Christina ~ Brunette Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=frankly-my-dear">frankly-my-dear</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=historical-romance-victorian">historical-romance-victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=victorian-mid-1851-1870">victorian-mid-1851-1870</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797535890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16269240283097060450"><br/>An elegant and bustling hotel in the heart of Victorian London, a lively heroine, an intriguingly remote hero, a meet-cute thanks to a mischievous ferret... and then it all went down the drain. Fast. <br/><br/>As of lately I haven’t been impressed with Kleypas’s recent series, The Ravenels, I decided to backlist among her older titles. Her books have always been a hit-or-miss with me, but since I’ve loved some of them in the past (probably <i>Dreaming of You</i> and <i>Devil in Winter</i> the most) and especially after</span>
  <span id="freeText16269240283097060450" style="display:none"><br />An elegant and bustling hotel in the heart of Victorian London, a lively heroine, an intriguingly remote hero, a meet-cute thanks to a mischievous ferret... and then it all went down the drain. Fast. <br /><br />As of lately I haven’t been impressed with Kleypas’s recent series, The Ravenels, I decided to backlist among her older titles. Her books have always been a hit-or-miss with me, but since I’ve loved some of them in the past (probably <i>Dreaming of You</i> and <i>Devil in Winter</i> the most) and especially after having enjoyed the Wallflowers series not too long ago, I went into The Hathaways with higher hopes. <br />At first I thought I’d found the same or similar mood and style that had previously worked, but soon the characters and storyline took a downward turn and never picked up, reminding me of all the reasons why The Ravenels have been such a letdown, the same problems outlined here as well.<br />Again a glaring uneven pace in the narration, with the slow-moving first 2/3 and then a rush to the end with added, apparently indispensable, absurd plot-twist in the very last pages. Again more or less clichéd characterisations with often exasperated traits. Yes, there were some sparse endearing moments, but as a whole the constant lack of meaningful communication and the juvenile push-and-pull between the leads ruined it for me.<br /><br />The moment Harry sees Poppy he goes into "Mine! Want!" mode, though in a sophisticated caveman (!) obsessive kind of way, and what ensues is a manipulation-fest in which our hero brazenly disregard the heroine’s feelings, who’s supposedly in love with another man for half the book, scheming and plotting to trap her into accepting his marriage proposal in the span of a few weeks. A hero whose sudden redemption I am then inveigled to believe because he doesn’t know how to express his finer feelings, but you see the heroine’s lurv will teach him and love cures all!... Well, you get the idea. <br />Instead I was wincing and shaking my head through most of their exchanges, from the awkward sex-scenes to the corny dialogues, which as a side note also sounded way too contemporary to ring true, while Poppy wavered between quirky and doormat all along. There was nothing romantic or spontaneous in the development of their relationship, no real humour, chemistry or self-awareness. <br />A cast of predictable and trite secondary characters and a pointless epilogue completed the picture. <br /><br />So the two stars go solely to the technically solid prose and to the fact that I managed to get interested enough to read on in order to see where this was going, though in a detached and dispassionate manner.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16269240283097060450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107390995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107390995" />
    <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish"><img alt="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398981306p2/1113032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107390995?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Historical Romance Lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=author-lisa-kleypas">author-lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=historical-romance-series">historical-romance-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=series-hathaways-kleypas">series-hathaways-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=abuse-physical-emotional-sexual">abuse-physical-emotional-sexual</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107390995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer577928698325761105"><br/>Harry Rutledge was both a neglected child and an abused child. The only son of an aging hotelier, Harry wasn’t raised in a home where a youngster could run and play, laugh out loud and just be a kid. Even at 5 years old he knew the rules: The Guests come first. Stay out of sight. Don’t make any noise. Don’t do this, don’t do that, don’t…don’t… don’t. Is it any wonder that as an adult, Harry is so rigid, so disciplined and so aloof? One of the richest men in London and one of the most mysterious,</span>
  <span id="freeText577928698325761105" style="display:none"><br />Harry Rutledge was both a neglected child and an abused child. The only son of an aging hotelier, Harry wasn’t raised in a home where a youngster could run and play, laugh out loud and just be a kid. Even at 5 years old he knew the rules: The Guests come first. Stay out of sight. Don’t make any noise. Don’t do this, don’t do that, don’t…don’t… don’t. Is it any wonder that as an adult, Harry is so rigid, so disciplined and so aloof? One of the richest men in London and one of the most mysterious, he often comments that his enemies like him better than his friends do.<br /><br />Poppy Hathaway is in her third London Season and as in the past, the family has taken rooms at the Rutledge Hotel because their home, Ramsay house, is too far away to travel to and from the many balls, parties and other events the Season has to offer. But following the Hathaways like mischief and misfortune often does, Poppy has found herself in an awkward position when Dodger the ferret, one of Beatrix’s pets, is on the loose in the hotel with a very important letter, one that simply must not be seen by anyone. It’s from a man who, if word got out of his affections for Poppy, would likely find himself in hot water with his father. His very rich, pompous, demanding and manipulative father – who would take away his title, his properties and everything else a man of the <i>ton</i> must have.<br /><br />And who do you suppose happens to run across Poppy in her pursuit of this rambunctious rodent? Why, none other than Harry Rutledge who finds himself more than a little captivated by Miss Hathaway and her furry friend. And so this is where the story begins. Will Poppy allow herself to be wooed by this man who no one really knows and can Harry allow her that part of himself he’s never given to anyone before - <i>his heart</i>?<br /><br />I think I’ve decided that Poppy is probably the most “normal” of all the Hathaways, and Harry Rutledge the most “normal” of all the men in their lives. Good thing they found each other or they probably would have gone through life alone because I can’t imagine anyone, except themselves, who would put up with the each other. Did that make any sense at all?<br /><br />And I was thinking… now, stay with me here… it seems as though the males in most historical romance novels have serious issues. So let’s explore the criteria for being a great hero, shall we?<br /><br />1.	They can’t be tamed. <br />2.	They’re into trouble all the time.<br />3.	Always taunting the women around them.<br />4.	All about having a good time. <br />5.	Charming.<br />6.	You just want to hold them.<br />7.	Adorable<br />8.	Handsome or at least cute.<br />9.	Maybe unsure of their parentage.<br /><br />So, in keeping with these hero characteristics, I suggest that Dodger get his own story! Don’t ferrets deserve a <i>happily ever after,</i> too? And if there’s any ferret deserving of one, I’d say it’s Dodger! And with this in mind, I suggest we begin a letter writing campaign to see if we can encourage Ms. Kleypas to find it in her heart to give Dodger a book of his very own. I say she should call it called <i>Sleepless in the Slipper Box.</i> What say you, dear readers of this review?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="577928698325761105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_47834310" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47834310" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47834310?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=series">series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47834310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2695325833365350557">(4.5 Stars - Edit: Revised on further consideration to 5 Stars)<br/><br/>I really enjoyed Harry and Poppy’s story. But I did feel there was a little something missing, hence the 4.5 Stars. (Edit: But now in looking back, I can't bear <i>not</i> to give 5 Stars to each and every Hathaway book, so while I acknowledge there was a little something "missing", I loved it and will definitely read it again!)<br/><br/>I especially loved how the description of Harry Rutledge conjured images of Richard Armitage. *sighs* He's so vill</span>
  <span id="freeText2695325833365350557" style="display:none">(4.5 Stars - Edit: Revised on further consideration to 5 Stars)<br><br>I really enjoyed Harry and Poppy’s story. But I did feel there was a little something missing, hence the 4.5 Stars. (Edit: But now in looking back, I can't bear <i>not</i> to give 5 Stars to each and every Hathaway book, so while I acknowledge there was a little something "missing", I loved it and will definitely read it again!)<br><br>I especially loved how the description of Harry Rutledge conjured images of Richard Armitage. *sighs* He's so villanously handsome and sexy! ^_^ <br><br><i>"He had heavy, well-cut hair, black as midnight, and a fair complexion in which his dark brows stood out in striking contrast. And he was handsome as Lucifer, his brows strong, his nose straight and defined, the mouth brooding. The angle of his jaw was sharp, tenacious, anchoring the grave features of a man who took everything - including himself - too seriously."</i><br><br>I was a <i>wee</i> bit annoyed with Harry through parts of the book, but I do love him and LOVED his declarations. He was so determined to win Poppy, no matter what. And to be compared to a "mechanism"? How can one resist?! LOL <br><br>Edited to add the quote (Copied from Dina's review - Thanks, Dina! ^_^):<br><br><i>"I want you any way I can get you. Not because you’re beautiful or clever or kind or adorable, although the devil knows you’re all those things. I want you because there’s no one else like you, and I don’t ever want to start a day without seeing you." <br><br>As Poppy opened her mouth to reply, he smoothed his thumb across her lower lip, coaxing her to wait until he had finished. "Do you know what a balance wheel is?" <br><br>She shook her head slightly. <br><br>"There’s one in every clock or watch. It rotates back and forth without stopping. It’s what makes the ticking sound... what makes the hands move forward to mark the minutes. Without it, the watch wouldn’t work. You’re my balance wheel, Poppy."</i> *SIGHS* <br><br>I think the something “missing”, for me, may have been how fast (time-wise) it seemed that Poppy and Harry resolved their issues? Or the seeming lack of build-up/tension in the middle of the book? And also, the suspense towards the end seemed unnecessary, to me. Although, going back to the resolution of that, I realised it was to tie back to the "fairy tale" metaphor. I did enjoy the cliff-hanger lead-in to Leo’s book though. Makes me even more excited and eager to read it!<br><br>Overall, though, I really did enjoy the book. I loved all the scenes with the Hathaway family. I <i>adore</i> this family! I laughed out loud quite a bit in this book. The Rutledge Hotel staff’s discussions were funny, especially the "vegetable-talk". *wiggles eyebrows* Can’t wait for Leo and Cat’s story! Look forward to finding out her secret past and what happened between Leo and Cat (maybe something compromising that they will end up “Married by Morning”??) Also, looking forward to Beatrix’s book, Love in the Afternoon! Can’t wait til “Summer 2010”! Thanks, LK, for 2 Hathaway books to look forward to in one year! ^_^<br><br>My Harry Rutledge (Richard Armitage):<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380321821i/690242.jpg" width="385" height="295" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379739019i/63938.jpg" width="375" height="285" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380321821i/690243.jpg" width="290" height="410" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379738196i/59972.jpg" width="365" height="365" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379738196i/59973.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379743178i/82552._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*siiiiigghhsss*<br><br>Yes, I know, I KNOW! I went a bit overboard with the Richard Armitage pics! LOL But I just ADORE this man. *<i>MELTS</i>* <br><br><br><br><i>COPYRIGHT DISCLAIMER: I do not hold the copyright to any of the images used in this review. They are posted to add visuals to the review and for fun. If any of these images are yours and you would like me to remove them, please let me know, and I will do so as soon as possible. If I can identify the copyright, I will do so.</i><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8513577703933339004"><b> ***5.0 "The Villian always gets the girl" stars***</b><br/>I absolutely love the Hathaways!!! And Harry and Poppy are the best!!!<br/><b>
  <blockquote>“In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it's possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.” </blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Harry</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553912836i/27288087._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='224' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I stayed up all night reading to finish this book. I loved Cam and Amelia, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6264710.Tempt_Me_at_Twilight__The_Hathaways___3_' title='Tempt Me at Twilight (The Hathaways, #3) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tempt Me at Twilight</a> turned out to be my favorite of the series. Cam was so damn perfect. I mean there wasn't a thing wrong wit</span>
  <span id="freeText8513577703933339004" style="display:none"><b> ***5.0 "The Villian always gets the girl" stars***</b><br>I absolutely love the Hathaways!!! And Harry and Poppy are the best!!!<br><b>
  <blockquote>“In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it's possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.” </blockquote>
</b><br><b>Harry</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553912836i/27288087._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I stayed up all night reading to finish this book. I loved Cam and Amelia, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6264710.Tempt_Me_at_Twilight__The_Hathaways___3_" title="Tempt Me at Twilight (The Hathaways, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Tempt Me at Twilight</a> turned out to be my favorite of the series. Cam was so damn perfect. I mean there wasn't a thing wrong with him. Whereas Harry was flawed in a way that pulled at my heart!<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I've never wanted to be loved. And God Knows no one's done it yet.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I love this family and Beatrix always makes me laugh so hard! She's the very opposite of lady like, but so darn practical and observant.<br><br><b><blockquote>“And Poppy, remember that someday you will meet a frog who will turn into a handsome prince."<br>"Good," Beatrix said. "Because all she's met so far are princes who turn into frogs."</blockquote>
<br><br><br>Poppy</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553912836i/27288088._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Poppy is naturally sweet and kind. But when she is forced into a marriage with a man she doesn't love, she doesn't mince words. She wasn't a doormat for Harry to walk all over and I loved that about her. She had that smug confident Harry feeling unsure and insecure.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553912836ra/27288089.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The Hathaways give me such joy. They are unconventional and carefree. They love and support each other. And they make me laugh when I least expect it!<br><br>Best Laugh out loud moment of the book:<br><br><b>“Did it fall out?" Leo asked. "Is she bald?"<br>"No, not at all. It's just that her hair is...green."<br>To look at Leo's face, one would think it was Christmas morning. "What shade of green?"<br>"Leo, hush," Win said urgently. "You are not to torment her. It's been a very trying experience. We mixed a peroxide paste to take the green out, and I don't know if it worked or not. Amelia was helping her to wash it a little while ago. And no matter what the result is, you are to say nothing."<br>"You're telling me that tonight, Marks will be sitting at the supper table with hair that matches the asparagus, and I'm not supposed to remark on it?" He snorted. "I'm not that strong."</b><br><br><br>Oh and that Epilogue has me craving the next book!! Finally, Leo and Cat!!!</span>

<div id="review_1342031239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342031239" />
    <a title="NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books"><img alt="NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528808758p2/37314676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342031239?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}" href="/user/show/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books">NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books?shelf=historical-romance-etc">historical-romance-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
