        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342031239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16670276940300698284"><b>
  <i>Okay, there is something above adoration??? <br/>Because i can assure you that i'm crazy about the Hathaways and their mates.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400731ra/776976.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Every book is a new apocalypse and i'm never satisfied... <br/>I want more and more and more...</i>
</b><br/><br/>Is it possible every story to be loved more than the previous??? For me, it is!!!<br/>The first book worked as an introduction for me and then i fell in love with Ken and Win and i thought that this couple was my favorite... <br/>But now after this book i think my favorite couple is Poppy and H</span>
  <span id="freeText16670276940300698284" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Okay, there is something above adoration??? <br>Because i can assure you that i'm crazy about the Hathaways and their mates.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400731ra/776976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Every book is a new apocalypse and i'm never satisfied... <br>I want more and more and more...</i>
</b><br><br>Is it possible every story to be loved more than the previous??? For me, it is!!!<br>The first book worked as an introduction for me and then i fell in love with Ken and Win and i thought that this couple was my favorite... <br>But now after this book i think my favorite couple is Poppy and Harry...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413139132ra/11470316.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>But i think that i have to finish and the two next books and after to stable in which one of them i love more... <br>But i'm pretty sure that i will love them all for different reasons...<br>And i really loved Poppy and Harry....<br><br>Poppy was the most quiet from the Hathaways. <br>She knew that her family was noisy and eccentric and she was seeking a normal life.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412711246ra/11411707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For the last three years, she was seeking for a husband and when she finally thought that she found the perfect man that she will offer her the calmness and normality that she was longing for, a ferret complicated her life....<br>Why a ferret??? You remember Dodget??? He was Beatrix's pet... <br>A ferret who stole many things for fun and one of that was a love letter for Poppy and that fact forced her to chased him all over the Rutledge hotel...<br>And she got to adventures since she met the unknown, mysterious and handsome Harry Rutledge, the owner of the hotel... <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438003707ra/15655039.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>And Harry was charmed so much by her that he manage to stole a kiss that change the course of their lives...<br><br>Harry wasn't believe in love. <br>His past prove him that love wasn't exist...<br>He was intelligent, beautiful and very successfull businessman. He had a brilliant mind that never stop working... <br>He didn't like publicity too much and he never wasted a glance to Poppy Hathaway before they come face to face and heard her talk unstopable about things that no other woman could talk!!!<br>And that was his condemnation... He was infatuated by her and he couldn't let her married someone else.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438003707ra/15655041.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So his dominate, manipulating and ruthless nature took action and twisted the things into his favor until to earn what he desired. Poppy Hathaway as his wife...<br>So he involved her in a scandal to persuade her that the best for her was to proceed in a marriage with him... and he worked very hard to succeeded...<br>But when Poppy found out the truth, she became furious with him and her stubborness got between them with intensity... <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438003707ra/15655042.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>So Harry had to change his ways to earn his wife back...<br><br>I won't lie to you. I love the complicating characters and Harry became my favorite...<br>I liked his anorthodox ways to take what he wants... and i liked the fact that he was honest.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438003707ra/15655043.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>From the first moment he warned Poppy about him... He never presented himself as the prince charming but he described him as the villain...<br>I liked his transition from the villain to a "dark" prince and i liked the way that he welcomed this unknown feeling that they called "love"...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438003707i/15655046._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And i think that he fitted quite perfect with the Hathaways... He finally found the family that he never had... <br><br>As for Poppy, i liked her as all the other Hathaways. <br>She was different and lovely. She was sensitive and she was caring for everyone.<br>And i know that from the first moment, Harry charmed her more that the"perfect" Michael... <br>But her mind was stucked in the idea that Michael could give her a perfect and easygoing life and when everything turned out differently that she was expecting, she prefered to accuse Harry and to fighting her feeling for him.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418857369ra/12923975.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But they were so perfect and lovely together... <br>The princess that manage to love a villain who thought that he was worthless of love...<br>A villain that manage to concrete the heart of a princess...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438003707ra/15655045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Damn!!! With that epilogue how can you not continue to Leo and Cat's story????<br>I'm so curious about what happened between them after all this phenomenal "hatred" between them!!!<br><b>I don't think i can ever stop reading about those strange and eccentric Hathaways!!! I love them!!</b></i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415071518ra/11721449.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219667556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer793466620225840748"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>"Perhaps Harry was becoming-or would become in time-the man he had always been meant to be. Because he had finally found someone who mattered."</b>
</blockquote><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514501684i/24784496._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='340' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> is the third book in The Hathaways Series. The series features the lives and trials of the Hathaway family. Each book can be read as a stand-alone. Set in 1852 in London, <b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> is the love story of Poppy Hathaway and the mysterious Harry Rutledge.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466701540i/19510149._SX540_.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"And whenever your wife is angry...for God's sake, don't try l</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText793466620225840748" style="display:none"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>"Perhaps Harry was becoming-or would become in time-the man he had always been meant to be. Because he had finally found someone who mattered."</b>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514501684i/24784496._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="340" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> is the third book in The Hathaways Series. The series features the lives and trials of the Hathaway family. Each book can be read as a stand-alone. Set in 1852 in London, <b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> is the love story of Poppy Hathaway and the mysterious Harry Rutledge.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466701540i/19510149._SX540_.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"And whenever your wife is angry...for God's sake, don't try logic."</b>
</blockquote> Poppy has been a loyal sister to her family. Working hard to be a lady, she has been secretly courting an Englishman in hopes that his family will be willing to accept her and he can take her as his wife. When Poppy accidentally meets Harry Rutledge, the owner of the hotel her family is staying in, Harry sets his sights on Poppy. In order to win her over, he will do whatever it takes to make her his. As Poppy is placed in an impossible position, she knows her only choice is to accept Harry's proposal and leave her love behind. Harry is an impossible man who has always been able to solve any problem. When the problem he needs to solve is winning over his wife, the predicament proves to be more than he could have ever imagined.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514500369i/24784329.jpg" width="500" height="340" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>"Love, there's hardly any place it can't be done. Against trees or walls, in chairs or bathtubs, on staircases or tables...balconies, carriages-"</b>
</blockquote> Told in dual POV, <b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b> is a romantic tale set back in time where reputation is everything. The plot is complex as Poppy must learn what it means to be a wife to a man who has never experienced love. I adored her spunk and tenacity throughout each and every moment. Poppy and Harry are stunning together and the dynamics between the push and pull they both experienced was intense and quite enjoyable. The relationships between the Hathaway family is truly remarkable as they love and protect each other fiercely. I was so taken by all of the characters, I decided that I must invest more time in this world immediately. The picturesque setting is described in such detail that I felt as if I had been transported back in time. One might assume that passion did not exist back in those times and yet, Harry and Poppy, I feared, would set my Kindle on fire! Lisa Kleypas has created a beautiful world with unforgettable characters. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466701540i/19510149._SX540_.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I never imagined myself to become a fan of Historical Romance and yet Lisa Kleypas has made me a believer! I am so thankful to my friend SueBee who introduced me to Harry and Poppy. I look forward to reading all of the Hathaway Series. A trip back in time has never been more sexy and sweet!<br><br><b>*This was an (F)BR with my girl SUEBEE in honor of HiShhtorical Week on Shh...!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511657057ra/24534160.gif" width="300" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" <span id="freeTextContainer6801270618709454842"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it's possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.” </i> </b><br/><br/>Not bad.... but also not amazing. I've been on a Lisa Kleypas binge and I'm on the Hathaway's series. I actually am liking it more than the Wallflowers (please don't throw the tomatoes!) but this one wasn't as good as the others. I'm not saying it was bad either, but it fits perfectly into a 3.5 rating where I did enjoy </span>
  <span id="freeText6801270618709454842" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “In the fairy tale you mentioned last night, I would probably be the villain. But it's possible the villain would treat you far better than the prince would have.” </i> </b><br><br>Not bad.... but also not amazing. I've been on a Lisa Kleypas binge and I'm on the Hathaway's series. I actually am liking it more than the Wallflowers (please don't throw the tomatoes!) but this one wasn't as good as the others. I'm not saying it was bad either, but it fits perfectly into a 3.5 rating where I did enjoy the book, but it's nothing special to me.<br><br>The premise is amazing, a secretive rich hotel owner falls in love with Poppy Hathaway and will literally do anything to have her. Tricked into a marriage she didn't expect, Poppy tries to make the best of her situation, but may be dealing with a man she doesn't understand.<br><br>I thought this was a sweet story, but it really could have been developed a lot better than it was. It went from distrust to love way too quickly to me. I felt we could have gotten more on Harry's background to understand how he was. But it felt like one sob story and one confession and suddenly everything was resolved.<br><br>I am very much looking forward to the next book because it's Leo and Miss Marks, hopefully it lives up to my expectations.<br><br><b> <i> “I want you any way I can get you. Not because you’re beautiful or clever or kind or adorable, although devil knows you’re all those things. I want you because there’s no one else like you, and I don’t ever want to start a day without seeing you.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494101706i/22685352._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Follow me on ♥ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ♥ <a href="http://rachelsreadsravenously.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="http://instagram.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/rayliz89" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343670638" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17233154044756889510"><b>4 The Princess and The Villain Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Harry. You’re not supposed to court a girl by telling her you’re the villain.”-Poppy</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/thats-wonderful_zps9dp8qpsz.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/><b>****Spoilers****</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I’m sure I’ve read too many fairy tales. The prince is supposed to slay the dragon, defeat the villain, and marry the servant girl, and carry her off to his castle.” “Fairy tales are best read as entertainment,” Harry said. “Not as a guide to life.” -Poppy and Harry</b>
</i> <br/><br/>Temp Me At Twilight, the 3rd book in The Hathaway Series, was a great read. 3 books</span>
  <span id="freeText17233154044756889510" style="display:none"><b>4 The Princess and The Villain Stars</b><br><br><i>
  <b>“Harry. You’re not supposed to court a girl by telling her you’re the villain.”-Poppy</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/thats-wonderful_zps9dp8qpsz.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460805757ra/18790165.gif" alt=" photo thats-wonderful_zps9dp8qpsz.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>****Spoilers****</b><br><br><i>
  <b>“I’m sure I’ve read too many fairy tales. The prince is supposed to slay the dragon, defeat the villain, and marry the servant girl, and carry her off to his castle.” “Fairy tales are best read as entertainment,” Harry said. “Not as a guide to life.” -Poppy and Harry</b>
</i> <br><br>Temp Me At Twilight, the 3rd book in The Hathaway Series, was a great read. 3 books into this series and I am still all smiles. What can I say I love the Hathaways. Every one of them. And with each new book I read in this series my love for them grows. I love that even though Poppy and Harry's love story starts out rough, and Harry wasn't really a sweet romance guy that I still fell in love with this couple. And I love that their love story starts with a mischievous ferret.<br><br><i>
  <b>“If I were going to molest you,” he pointed out, “I would have done so by now.” Her flush deepened at his bluntness. “So you say. But for all I know, you could be a very slow molester.”-Harry and Poppy</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/tumblr_n1oaxzFPdm1sioa7wo1_500_zps5hytspcy.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460808073ra/18790798.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n1oaxzFPdm1sioa7wo1_500_zps5hytspcy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“You were courted by a boy, who had to do as he was told.” His hot breath feathered against her lips as he whispered, “You should try it with a man, who needs no one’s permission.”-Harry</b>
</i><br><br>I really enjoyed that the hero was more of a villain in this book. Harry wanted Poppy so much that he wasn't above cheating, stealing, and fighting dirty to have her. Harry met Poppy after Bea's ferret ran off with a love letter from Michael to Poppy. Harry wanted Poppy and when he found out Poppy had feelings for another man, Michael(who had been secretly dating Poppy because his father wouldn't approve of the match) he did what any good, kindhearted man would...... He told Michael's daddy! Daddy disapproved and Michael being the little bitch that he was didn't fight for Poppy, but instead broke up with her. Leaving Harry to swoop in and take her. I loved that Harry wasn't your typical hero. Harry had been raised with no love and neglected so he didn't show emotions. He came off as cold, selfish, and hard at first. But as the story goes on you can't help but fall in love with him. I also loved that even though he softens with Poppy's love, he never regrets how he stole Poppy from Michael. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I’m everything they told you and worse,” Harry said without hesitation. “But what they didn’t tell you is that you are the most desirable and fascinating woman I’ve ever met, and I would do anything to have you.”-Harry </b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/286459a_zpsxkz6j1yo.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460805757i/18790167._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 286459a_zpsxkz6j1yo.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I will never forget that you took away the man I loved and put yourself in his place. I’m not certain I can ever forgive you for that. The only thing I am absolutely certain of is that I will never love you. Do you still want to marry me?” “Yes,” Harry said without hesitation. “I’ve never wanted to be loved. And God knows no one’s done it yet.”-Poppy and Harry</b>
</i><br><br>Poppy just wanted a normal, calm life. She thought she would have that with Michael. She loved Michael and it crushed her that he broke off their relationship. When she went to a ball to show everyone that she wasn't Michael's off cast she ends up dancing with Harry. Getting upset and not wanting to cry in front of everyone she asked Harry to take her for fresh air. While outside Harry kissed Poppy and they were seen. Leaving Poppy with the choice to be a fallen woman or to marry Harry. She married Harry even after finding out about Harry telling Michael's father, but deceit made for a rough marriage. I loved that it took awhile for Poppy to give her heart to Harry. She didn't just forgive him and hop into his bed. She didn't even kiss him. And she let her displeasure of his actions be known. But Poppy was a loving, happy kind of person and the more she was around Harry and saw the real him when he let his walls down the more she fell in love with her husband. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I can’t. I’ll never be sorry about it. Because if I hadn’t done it, you’d be his now. And he only wanted you if it was easy for him. But I want you any way I can get you. Not because you’re beautiful or clever or kind or adorable, although the devil knows you’re all those things. I want you because there’s no one else like you, and I don’t ever want to start a day without seeing you.”-Harry</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/17185523_zpsn7d60sz7.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460805757ra/18790168.gif" alt=" photo 17185523_zpsn7d60sz7.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I want you to be happy, you exasperating man. I want you to understand that I love you for exactly what you are.”-Poppy</b>
</i><br><br>I loved that Harry and Poppy's love was slower to come. The lust was there but Harry had to earn her trust. When the love came it was beautiful, full of passion, and kindness. Love changed Harry for the better. I will be honest, I didn't feel the least bit sorry for Poppy's ex Michael. A real man wouldn't let daddy stop him from being with the woman he loved. I couldn't stand Michael. I thought he was a coward, and was glad that after Poppy married Harry, he suffered. Just sayin! I loved getting to see the other Hathaways in this book and getting to catch up with Cam, Amelia, and their son. There was some big and happy news for Kev and Win too. I was really enjoying the playing between Cat and Leo. I'm excited to start their book. I missed Bea a bit as she and her animal freak show kinda took a backseat in this book. Bea's story is the one I am looking forward to most. Great read, great series!!<br><br><i>
  <b>“Because I have so much to lose now. But I’m going to love you anyway, because there doesn’t seem to be any way to stop doing it.” He kissed her forehead, eyelids, cheeks. “I have so much love for you, I could fill rooms with it. Buildings. You’re surrounded by it wherever you go, you walk through it, breathe it . . . it’s in your lungs, and under your tongue, and between your fingers and toes . . .”-Harry</b>
</i><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsession.blogspot.com/2017/04/tempt-me-at-twilight.html">http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsessio...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17233154044756889510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540786201?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=regency-victorian-era">regency-victorian-era</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540786201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer405564841526752793"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas' title='Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lisa Kleypas</a> was my introduction to the Historical Romance genre, and to this day, the vast majority of such books I read are 'penned' by her. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43172-the-hathaways' rel='nofollow noopener'></a>The Hathaway series however has never really hit it off with me, so much so that I've never even read the last book of the series. An upopular opinion, if I were to look at GoodReads trends. <br/><br/>In contrast, when it came to the books from the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41154-wallflowers' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wallflower</a> series, I have read and <em>re</em>read them <em>numerous</em> times. Still suffering from holiday blues, unable to conce</span>
  <span id="freeText405564841526752793" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas" title="Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Kleypas</a> was my introduction to the Historical Romance genre, and to this day, the vast majority of such books I read are 'penned' by her. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43172-the-hathaways" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>The Hathaway series however has never really hit it off with me, so much so that I've never even read the last book of the series. An upopular opinion, if I were to look at GoodReads trends. <br><br>In contrast, when it came to the books from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41154-wallflowers" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wallflower</a> series, I have read and <em>re</em>read them <em>numerous</em> times. Still suffering from holiday blues, unable to concentrate on any of the other books I've started, I decided to try my luck with my favorite installment from The Hathaway series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546422207ra/26847963.gif" alt="determined sigh" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wily businessman Harry Ruthledge has set his heart on marrying. A chance encounter with the unconventional Poppy Hathaway convinces the mysterious hotel owner, that he just <em>has</em> to have the girl for his own. So he proceeds to woo her rather aggressively, even going so far as to skillfully remove Poppy's "<em>secret</em>" admirer.<br><br>Poppy for her part, bears he beau's sudden departure rather stoically, trying to make the best of her new suitor. Still, when she eventually finds out the truth, right before her wedding ceremony, she is not exactly thrilled. Demure and serious, our heroine still goes through with the wedding, vowing to repay her husband with as chilly a demeanor as possible.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546422207ra/26847964.gif" alt="quiet anger" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Despite all the excitement I recall from my first read, I was rather disappointed this time. Harry was basically a jerk, to whom young Poppy has to bow down. Good thing she doesn't really stand for his boorishness for too long, which also eventually prompts him to change himself.<br><br>Their chemistry was.... okay, I guess. Certainly not awful, but certainly nowhere near the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435890152" rel="nofollow noopener">excitement of Sebastian and Evie</a> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>. <br><br><strong>Score: 3/5 stars</strong><br><br>The reading experience was fine I guess, but it was definitely clear to me that I'm no longer interested in Regency romances. That being said, if <em>you</em> personally are a fan of the genre, then by all means give it a shot.<br>============================<br>Review of the 2nd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541412418" rel="nofollow noopener">Seduce Me at Sunrise</a><br>Review of the epilogue of the 2nd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541412844" rel="nofollow noopener">A Hathaway Wedding</a></span>

<div id="review_61449866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61449866" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61449866?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of LK's Devil In Winter</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=victorian-era">victorian-era</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61449866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5698181660113575278"> <i>Poppy Hathaway longs for a normal life, although she loves her very unconventional family, she wants something more stable and safe, when she falls in love with a man she thinks can bring her happiness, is heartbroken when he turns her away for his title which leads her into scandal and the arms of …<br/> Harry Rutledge, who is a well-known ruthless hotel owner, known to always gets what he wants “always” and when he lays eyes on Poppy he knows he must have her at any cost but when they marry they f</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5698181660113575278" style="display:none"> <i>Poppy Hathaway longs for a normal life, although she loves her very unconventional family, she wants something more stable and safe, when she falls in love with a man she thinks can bring her happiness, is heartbroken when he turns her away for his title which leads her into scandal and the arms of …<br /> Harry Rutledge, who is a well-known ruthless hotel owner, known to always gets what he wants “always” and when he lays eyes on Poppy he knows he must have her at any cost but when they marry they find they must learn to trust and break down their defenses to find the love their both have always seek…</i><br /><br /><br /> As I started to read this, I was quickly drawn into the story, with deep shades of LK’s Devil of Winter written all over it. If anyone could turn a villain into a beloved hero, LK could and she does it with true style and grace with Harry. <br /> <br /> Poppy is the only “normal” Hathaway, coming across as the kind caregiver of the family with a heart full of love and kindness. At first she comes across as narrow-minded in her views of love and what happiness is. She kept reaching for a safe haven in someone. She comes from her shelter when she’s heartbroken by her first love and then has to learn to trust as she falls in love with Harry. Because of her desire to want love and a safe marriage, Poppy was blinded by her first love and his faults. Harry opens her eyes to a bigger and better world, where she can have so much more. <br /><br /> Harry was a complex puzzle, a mechanical genius and ruthless hotel owner; he shows many sides, and keeping you guessing whom the real Harry is. I don’t think Harry even knew whom is really was. Always thinking and trying to have everything in his life in order, when things don’t go the way he wants he relies on the cold part of his mind to find a way to fix it or make it his. <br /> I really loved Harry, when he wanted something he took it with both hands by hook or crook. Did I agree with what he did was right? I do. He knew Poppy’s first love didn’t have the balls to take Poppy and if he really loved her and wanted her, he would risk it all. Poppy’s first love was given many chances, but he didn’t take it and became a wimpy baby because he missed his chance. <br /> If there was a man out there as hot as Harry who wanted me as much as Harry wanted Poppy- I tie myself up and tell him “take me away” <br /> Harry was drawn to Poppy due to her brightest and kindness something he lacked in his own life, and as his defenses are torn down, he starts to move away from his past hurts, he becomes his true self and finds his heart along the way.<br /><br /> The love scenes are few and far between, but in LK fashion are built up to and she doesn’t disappoint, as they are pretty hot and steamy.<br /> <br /> The Hathaway clan is still pretty pronounced through the story as Poppy turns to her family for advice and help. I loved the Hathaways and how tight knit they are and how they accept Harry into the family (even giving him some much needed advice along the way)<br /><br /> I felt what brought an overall awesome story down, what the sudden filler toward the end. If LK wanted a bigger word count, I feel leaving it out would have been better. <br /> Also the cliffhanger, what was that?! It didn’t feel like LK at all, almost like she was forced to add this. I really didn’t care for it as it brought the overall story down. I wouldn’t have minded a seek peek into the next book, but a cliffhanger was just plain stupid IMO.<br /><br /> Overall: an wonderful story, with great leads but could have done without the sudden filler and cliffhanger<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5698181660113575278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369643356?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollis " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollis " href="/user/show/16668577-hollis">Hollis </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8121948-tempt-me-at-twilight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=aar">aar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=all-the-feels">all-the-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=all-the-lols">all-the-lols</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=heroes-to-root-for">heroes-to-root-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=hist-romance">hist-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=rhr">rhr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=family-focused">family-focused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=swoony-crush-worthy-boys">swoony-crush-worthy-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369643356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6363515045412247394">This review can also be found at <a href='http://www.romantichistoricalreviews.com/retro-review-tempt-me-at-twilight-hathaways-3-by-lisa-kleypas/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Romantic Historical Reviews</a>.<br/><br/><b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b>, book three in Lisa Kleypas' <i>
  <b>The Hathaways</b>
</i> series, is a little different from the previous books in the sense that we're no longer dealing with a couple where one comes from a different, or diverse, background. Amelia and Winnifred both found themselves marrying Romany men (Romany men who happen to share more than just heritage in common, but that's a spoiler!) but it's Poppy, the pretty but socially awkward si</span>
  <span id="freeText6363515045412247394" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.romantichistoricalreviews.com/retro-review-tempt-me-at-twilight-hathaways-3-by-lisa-kleypas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Romantic Historical Reviews</a>.<br /><br /><b>Tempt Me at Twilight</b>, book three in Lisa Kleypas' <i>
  <b>The Hathaways</b>
</i> series, is a little different from the previous books in the sense that we're no longer dealing with a couple where one comes from a different, or diverse, background. Amelia and Winnifred both found themselves marrying Romany men (Romany men who happen to share more than just heritage in common, but that's a spoiler!) but it's Poppy, the pretty but socially awkward sister, who is looking for a partnership that is a little more conventional and more traditionally stable.<br /><br />Having grown up in a family of scholars, eccentrics, and unique personalities, all Poppy wants is to be normal. She doesn't begrudge her family for being who they are, but she wants less of the reputation of being one of 'those Hathaways' and instead wants a quiet family of her own. The problem is that for all her beauty, she's still one of 'those Hathaways' and as a result is awkward because she is intelligent and prefers to speak on topics most women her age know nothing about – or rather, know enough to not speak on, as is more appropriate. Nonetheless she's being covertly courted by a man she loves, and who loves her, and is only waiting for the right time to broach the subject with his father – a peer – and she feels her forever happiness is within her grasp.<br /><br />So, naturally, it's at this time that she stumbles into the path of Harry Rutlegde, the wealthy and rather mysterious owner of the famous Rutledge Hotel. Not knowing who he is, she charms him by being herself, intelligent and willing to speak about anything if given any encouragement, and Harry finds himself wanting her. Wanting her in the ways he wants all pretty and clever things. And like all men who are used to having, and getting, their way, he's not above manipulating matters to make it so that she will be his.<br /><br />Harry is ruthless, manipulative, and totally unapologetic about his machinations to ensnare Poppy. The way Kleypas writes him, at turns shining a light on his kindness, his willingness to court Poppy, and then twisting it so she's unable to refuse him, is.. well. I think that in the hands of another author, Harry would have been easy to hate. But he isn't at all. I was totally fascinated by him, just as Poppy was, and he really carried the story for me. He's relentless in keeping his hotel running, pushing his employees, pushing himself, and he's creative, inventing ways to improve all manner of tasks. He is certain he can never be loved, because he never had been, and so is not remotely dismayed to know that by having Poppy as his wife, he will have her body, but she will never give him her heart.<br /><br />Poppy, on the other hand, confused me. She's smart, kind, caring, but also.. I don't know. I couldn't envy her situation – torn from the man she wanted and bound to the one who caused her such upheaval – but at the same time, she's equally manipulative and also unkind to Harry. At least in the early to middle section of the story. But when they finally come together, when Harry is pushed into chasing her, when she lets him in.. they work. He's a man who needs so desperately to be loved, to be chosen, and Poppy eventually realizes he's the man she would choose above all others.<br /><br />The best part of this series, though, is that when there's a lull in the romance, or something irks me or doesn't work to my full satisfaction, there's the rest of the supporting cast ready to pick up the slack or distract me. Because this family is one of the best fictional families I've had the pleasure of reading about. Cam and Amelia (from book one, <b>Mine Till Midnight</b>) are present and being lovey-dovey and adorable with their new son. Winnifred and Merripen are still new-in-love and tender with each other. There's Leo, causing mischief yet also managing to be selfless and supportive when his sisters need him to be, all the time antagonizing the governess/family's companion (and hoo boy is there a nice surprise in Catherine's storyline!), and finally, Beatrice; who, even as the youngest, somehow manages to be insightful at the right times, adorable, and is always chasing after the mischief her array of pets gets into.<br /><br />For all that I've wanted to drag out my (belated) reading of this series, it's hard not to rush into the next book. They're compulsively enjoyable, with a good mix of emotional arcs, humour, heat, and sweetness. I'm so looking forward to seeing where this family ends up next. And as for that ending to set up Cat and Leo's book? You, Ms. Kleypas, are a dirty tease.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6363515045412247394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146704405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9051618805183570336">Re-read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1311998669?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lacey</a>, who unlike me, loved this! As did all my friends. Seriously, I'm not hating on anyone who loved this, I just couldn't stand this book.<br/><br/>Down-grated from four to one stars after re-reading it again after about 4 years. All I can say is, my tastes have changed dramatically since then. There are a few things I no longer tolerate, and Harry basically did everything in his power to piss me off. <br/><br/>a) He breaks off Poppy and the man she loves and is engaged to on a whim, uhm, because he</span>
  <span id="freeText9051618805183570336" style="display:none">Re-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1311998669?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lacey</a>, who unlike me, loved this! As did all my friends. Seriously, I'm not hating on anyone who loved this, I just couldn't stand this book.<br /><br />Down-grated from four to one stars after re-reading it again after about 4 years. All I can say is, my tastes have changed dramatically since then. There are a few things I no longer tolerate, and Harry basically did everything in his power to piss me off. <br /><br />a) He breaks off Poppy and the man she loves and is engaged to on a whim, uhm, because he "wants her more than the other guy". And therefore he deserves her more which makes it perfectly reasonable to go behind the other man's back and blacken Poppy's name with his pompous, blue-blood obsessed father who won't let his son marry a nobody. <br /><br />b) He's possessive, controlling, manipulative, and manages to make Poppy believe that everything that goes wrong in their relationship is her fault. No, I do not find him romantic. Apparently I'm in the minority with this... (And please don't get me started on his redemption. Too little, too late for me. Leo at least changed over the course of three books, but Harry did a complete 180 within the last four or so chapters.)<br /><br />c) The wedding night from hell and other things that made me furious: <br />Poppy sacrifices herself, saying she just "wants this over with". <br />Harry: "At least give this a chance." <br />Poppy: "I can't. Not when I remember that I should be doing this with him."<br />Harry: "Then I'll see if I can put him out of your thoughts..." The charming man then proceeds to touch a woman who would rather be with someone else. But, of course, we can't have him actually abuse her, so he stops at the last moment. Saying, "I won't force the rest of it on you tonight ... You want to have done with it so you'll have nothing more to dread. But I've decided to let you dread it a bit longer. Just remember that if you have any idea about requesting an annulment, I'll have you on your back and divested of your virginity before you can blink." <br /><br />A few days later:<br />Poppy: "If you keep your promise to Sir Gerald, I'm going to leave you." <br />Harry: "That's not a choice for you." ... Leave him, would she? Not in this life, or the next. She thought him a monster. Well, he would prove her right...<br />And then basically forces himself on her. But she loves it of course, so that's ok? He takes her virginity, she cries and is in pain, he walks out because he can't be bothered to deal with all those feelings, and she then proceeds to blame herself for his treatment. <br /><br />I could rant away about how I'm not ok with this, but I'm too tired. Suffice to say, I didn't think Harry was a mysterious, brooding anti-hero, I did not like him, I was not convinced by his redemption, and...<br /><br />Oh well. Now I'm off to re-read Leo's book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3022116713352828134">"just as a child of ten might act when you're far too old<br/><br/>You're not hopeless or helpless and I hate to sound cold...."<br/><br/>You know there are times the opening bars of this song ("You Don't Know What love Is (You Just Do as You're Told)," White Stripes if you aren't placing it) come up when I finish a romance and I have to figure out why. It just starts in my head. It fits many so well. Particularly those alpha holes. Well, this wasn't that for me.<br/><br/>My friend list is all over the map with this book. I'</span>
  <span id="freeText3022116713352828134" style="display:none">"just as a child of ten might act when you're far too old<br /><br />You're not hopeless or helpless and I hate to sound cold...."<br /><br />You know there are times the opening bars of this song ("You Don't Know What love Is (You Just Do as You're Told)," White Stripes if you aren't placing it) come up when I finish a romance and I have to figure out why. It just starts in my head. It fits many so well. Particularly those alpha holes. Well, this wasn't that for me.<br /><br />My friend list is all over the map with this book. I'm all over the map with this book. So...I get it.<br /><br />But is this romance? It was a great family drama and Leo *fans self* but how much are they going to steal the show? I love that my affection for Cam &amp; Amelia grows. (Kev, ick, get outta my face) and that the family dynamic is so well fleshed out I somehow come out liking these books even though the romance....<br /><br />Well, the romance sucked.<br /><br />"But you don't know what love is, you just do as you're told,"<br /><br />I didn't even mind Harry in the beginning. Broken assholes are my jam. Manipulating a situation, well, you know what, we do that on a daily basis to get our way. My husband made a ridiculous play for me when I was dating someone else. Whatever. I'm down. In fact, I obviously find it unbearably charming. What I struggled with was Poppy's odd personality. Loving family, full sense of self and no reason for insecurity that I'm aware of...she relegates herself, rather than to her family in Hampshire, to marrying a man who she sees as taking away her choice. (<i> You're not hopeless or helpless,</i><br /><br />So, um, what the fuck? Then she proceeds to punish him and asks him why he wants her so no less than 2 times. She makes him chase her....for what. Then the plot twist oh god, just make it end. Why is she so mudery and kidnappy in her plots. GIVE ME A BREAK.<br /><br />So in the end, Harry was a broken, manipulative, determined asshole who fell in love and grew a heart. And Poppy? Her growth? Didn't see it. Found her behavior just as abusive post marriage. "Oh yes ravage me. I will not have you hold anything over on me. We shall make this official but I will not participate." <br /><br />NO THANKS. F for the romance. ("All those empty I love yous") I did not understand the relationship. I understand them separately better. I understand Harry desiring Poppy. I even understand Poppy... But together. Bleh.<br /><br />A for the fam. <br /><br />That winds up as a solid 2-stars. Because this is romance, folks. I get my epic family drama elsewhere.</span>

<div id="review_123757059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123757059" />
    <a title="♥  Sam ♥ ~S2~Im made of awesomness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3209146-sam-s2-im-made-of-awesomness"><img alt="♥  Sam ♥ ~S2~Im made of awesomness" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299404961p2/3209146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123757059?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥  Sam ♥ ~S2~Im made of awesomness" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥  Sam ♥ ~S2~Im made of awesomness" href="/user/show/3209146-sam-s2-im-made-of-awesomness">♥  Sam ♥ ~S2~Im made of awesomness</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3209146-sam-s2-im-made-of-awesomness?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123757059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11403451392573682981"><b> This is not your ordinary review people! </b><br/><br/>I never imagined being so drawn into historical novels. NEVER.EVER. But Lisa Kleypas has done exactly that. I have been introduced into a world woman are treated different, men are superior and there are a different set of rules for everyone. It has captivated me to say the least. <br/><br/>But this got me thinking about what it <i> really </i> was like 150 years ago. These stories that we all read are all about balls, courting, dresses and chivalry but after taking a de</span>
  <span id="freeText11403451392573682981" style="display:none"><b> This is not your ordinary review people! </b><br><br>I never imagined being so drawn into historical novels. NEVER.EVER. But Lisa Kleypas has done exactly that. I have been introduced into a world woman are treated different, men are superior and there are a different set of rules for everyone. It has captivated me to say the least. <br><br>But this got me thinking about what it <i> really </i> was like 150 years ago. These stories that we all read are all about balls, courting, dresses and chivalry but after taking a deeper look I realized that life for woman (and men) in the 19th century was deplorable.<br><br>This is what the women looked like.<br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>No smiling you will notice. Why?? They properly all had horrible teeth, not to mention bad breath. Braces anyone??? NOT HERE PEOPLE!<br><br>* Toothpaste wasn't sold in paste form in tubed until late 1890's<br><br>*Soap? Only available to the wealthy.<br><br>*Did women even shave their legs or underarm?. Dont think so!<br><br>*Bathing and indoor plumbing? NOT LIKELY<br><br>*A woman wouldn't cut their hair. (My god if the word "style cut" wasn't in my vocabulary I think I would have an aneurism)<br><br>*Deodorant - B.O is not good regardless of wether you didnt know any better.<br><br>*Them HUGE skirts. Want to exercise, take a jog? NOPE!<br><br>*It was written into men and women's wedding vows that a man could demand and take sexual acts at any time he wanted regardless of how the woman felt. (Sorry gals no faking the headache in this era)<br><br>I could go on but I wont because Im bound to be bringing everyone down. But If I put all that aside and just enjoy the novels I can look past all the gross stuff and read a truly romantic novel. Where the men are handsome and overly protective of their loved one. Sex is a mutual consent and everyone one is filled with unbound passion.<br><br>This novel has that many reviews that im just going to say that I did love Poppy's book. Harry was a bit of a pompous arse for most of the book but of course he reprieved himself to be a perfect man.<br><br>Cannot wait for Leo and Catherine's book. That is going to be one exciting book!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11403451392573682981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60874578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60874578" />
    <a title="Juliana Philippa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1378820-juliana-philippa"><img alt="Juliana Philippa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597182219p2/1378820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60874578?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juliana Philippa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juliana Philippa" href="/user/show/1378820-juliana-philippa">Juliana Philippa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=romance-historical">romance-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=hr-series-book-3">hr-series-book-3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-own-in-dead-tree-form">0-own-in-dead-tree-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=hr-hero-businessman">hr-hero-businessman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-reviewed">0-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=hr-hero-difficult-childhood">hr-hero-difficult-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=2009-reads">2009-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=hr-heroine-unusual-odd">hr-heroine-unusual-odd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-read-multiple-times">0-read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=2009-sep-reads">2009-sep-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60874578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14957555489971284725"><blockquote>
  <i>She cleared her throat and sighed shortly. “Forgive me. I talk excessively. I shouldn’t—”<br/><br/>“No,” Harry said, overwhelmed by a baffling and unfamiliar emotion, white-knuckled with it. “I could listen to you all day.”</i>
</blockquote><b>A solid Kleypas read with a wonderful "villain" hero and another charming Hathaway sister <i>(cycling rating: 4 stars to 3.5 stars to 4 stars)</i></b><br/><br/>At last!! Another Kleypas novel - now we all just have to survive the wait for the story we've all been waiting for: Leo and "Marks" (or Catheri</span>
  <span id="freeText14957555489971284725" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She cleared her throat and sighed shortly. “Forgive me. I talk excessively. I shouldn’t—”<br /><br />“No,” Harry said, overwhelmed by a baffling and unfamiliar emotion, white-knuckled with it. “I could listen to you all day.”</i>
</blockquote><b>A solid Kleypas read with a wonderful "villain" hero and another charming Hathaway sister <i>(cycling rating: 4 stars to 3.5 stars to 4 stars)</i></b><br /><br />At last!! Another Kleypas novel - now we all just have to survive the wait for the story we've all been waiting for: Leo and "Marks" (or Catherine/Cat, which we learn in this novel is her first name). I completely agree with the reviewer Luckee that this book was definitely satisfying and enjoyable, but there was just a little something missing. Is it worth rushing out to your nearest bookstore and buying though? Yes. Will you be left feeling giddy after you read it? Yes. And are there the classic characters we all love, the chemistry Kleypas excels at writing, and the humorous and witty scenes we adore? Yes. So basically: yes, buy it, steal it, whatever, but read it!<br /><br /><b>MAIN CHARACTERS</b><br /><b>Harry Rutledge (early 30s)</b> is a wonderful hero - the kind of bad-guy-whom-we-love-to-love hero that Kleypas created for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/330721.Dreaming_of_You__The_Gamblers_of_Craven_s___2_" title="Dreaming of You (The Gamblers of Craven's, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreaming of You</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/109580.Where_Dreams_Begin" title="Where Dreams Begin by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Where Dreams Begin</a>. Harry is ruthless, complex, very emotionally closed-off, and will stop at nothing to get what he wants - which usually comes very easily to him now. However he's also fair, humorous, extremely hardworking and intelligent, intense, passionate, loyal, and can be extremely tender and sensitive.<br /><br />Here LK has created a "hero" à la Sebastian, Lord St. Vincent (from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>), because as Harry himself says in the scene that was being used as the teaser-excerpt: in this story, it's the villain of the fairy-tale who gets the princess, not the prince. Harry definitely does some questionable things, though I would say that Kleypas does a very good job of having her character toe the line, but never quite crossing it - and writing him in such a way that one can't help but understand why Poppy is so attracted and drawn to him, because frankly what woman wouldn't be?! Basically, you know him ... he's the bad/cold guy who just secretly (even unconsciously) wants to love and cuddle / be loved and cuddled but was - surprise, surprise - just waiting (even if he didn't know it) for the right woman to come along. Let's not even pretend that we don't all (or okay, to be fair, *most* all of us) absolutely **LOVE** this type of hero, lol.<br /><br /><b>Poppy Hathaway (23)</b> is a great counterbalance to Harry - as he so eloquently puts it in one scene in the book when he compares her to a clock mechanism ;-). She's charming, friendly, outgoing, loving, intelligent, and a wonderful conversationalist (sounds like a mundane attribute, but really isn't in this case) who is interested by almost everything and everyone. All Poppy has ever wanted is a calm and quiet life - something not often found in the Hathaway household - with a partner whom she loves, and though she thinks she has found this in the form of Michael Bayning, Harry maneuvers everything so that ... well, let's just say that path becomes somewhat obstructed for Poppy.<br /><br />I liked Poppy's freshness and honesty - there is no guile with her and it's easy to see why someone like Harry (or anyone, for that matter) would be drawn to her. One of the things I loved best about Poppy was that she wasn't written as being so perfect that it was almost hard to like her or feel any kinship with her; she has flaws - though admittedly not as many as Harry, lol - and there's one scene in particular where after speaking with Leo about something, she decides that she was in the wrong and is going to apologize. If you want to know what other LK heroines she's most like, I would probably say a combination of Sara Fielding (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/330721.Dreaming_of_You__The_Gamblers_of_Craven_s___2_" title="Dreaming of You (The Gamblers of Craven's, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreaming of You</a>) for her honesty and friendliness, Daisy Bowman (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105574.Scandal_in_Spring__Wallflowers___4_" title="Scandal in Spring (Wallflowers, #4) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Scandal in Spring</a>) for her simplicity and positivity, and Charlotte Howard (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114168.Worth_Any_Price__Bow_Street_Runners___3_" title="Worth Any Price (Bow Street Runners, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Worth Any Price</a>) for how her relationship with the hero is portrayed and in the way that he needs/wants her.<br /><br /><b>OTHER COMMENTS.</b> We see lots of the whole Hathaway clan (and are given great teasers about Leo and Marks, see P.S. for more details) and the staff of the Rutledge Hotel are great additions to the book. They really add to the story, as well as giving further depth to Harry and the relationship he develops with Poppy. They also provide some wonderful humor, which is always a great thing for any romance book, and this book definitely has some of the LOL scenes that I always come to treasure in LK's novels - one of the greatest ones is when the hotel top-staff are in the kitchen discussing the intimate side (or lack thereof) of Harry and Poppy's relationship and the chef is making all these vegetable metaphors. :-))) Couldn't stop laughing!<br /><br /><b>CRITICISM.</b> The "there's-something-missing-but-I'm-not-exactly-sure-what" factor is hard to describe because, yes, I'm not exactly sure what it is. The whole relationship feels somewhat rushed to me and takes place over a shorter period of time than I feel is usually used in Kleypas' books (at least in her historicals). Because they know each other for so little time and the period (time-wise) that the book covers is somewhat on the short side, I think that the development of their relationship seems a little rushed or stilted, not containing as much plausible depth as some of Kleypas' other main characters, and problems that dog the story and their marriage seem to conclude almost too quickly right before the end.<br /><br />Also, although the chemistry between Harry and Poppy is definitely there, it's not AS shimmery/practically-tangible as in some of her other novels. Compared to a lot of other authors out there, it's still absolutely wonderful and excellently written when it is there and you definitely will NOT feel like you were short-changed on the romance part - however compared to the first two Hathaway books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693016.Mine_Till_Midnight__The_Hathaways___1_" title="Mine Till Midnight (The Hathaways, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine Till Midnight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2948832.Seduce_Me_at_Sunrise__The_Hathaways___2_" title="Seduce Me at Sunrise (The Hathaways, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Seduce Me at Sunrise</a>), it just was not as "charged."<br /><br />Finally, most authors have to include some mystery/villain twist at the end and LK provides this obligatory plot twist. I myself thought it seemed a bit superfluous and could have been done without, but no more details since then I would have to include spoilers.<br /><br /><b>BOTTOM LINE.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6264710.Tempt_Me_at_Twilight__The_Hathaways___3_" title="Tempt Me at Twilight (The Hathaways, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Tempt Me at Twilight</a> is still a great read, and I definitely do NOT regret rushing out this morning and buying it at the nearest bookstore (my apologies, Amazon.com). We're teased at the end that Summer 2010 will see - get this - TWO NEW HISTORICAL ROMANCES by LK. Yes, I know, take a moment to sit down, take a deep breath, and collect yourself (... or was that just my reaction?). They are the remaining two books in the Hathaway series: <i>Married by Morning</i> and <i>Love In the Afternoon</i>.<br /><br /><b>P.S. FOR ALL THE LEO AND MISS MARKS FANS (i.e. everyone in existence who is aware of them)</b><br />The rumor is that <i>Married by Morning</i> is Leo's story (and Marks/Catherine/Cat's, because really, it's just too cruel to even IMAGINE she's not his heroine) and will be the next Hathaway book released - I don't know about the rest of you, but even the thought of the Leo/Cat story has me jumping up and down like a kid in a candy store (but no pressure LK, lol). As other reviews mention, this book is choc-a-bloc FULL of little teasers and further developments in their relationship (plus some new and *very interesting* disclosures about Cat's past - though still not everything, of course). Whenever their book finally DOES come out, it will be an absolute must to reread the previous Hathaway books first so the anticipation can really build ... and then we can just wallow in enjoyment, lol. I can (seriously) barely contain my excitement - good to know I have a whole ~10 months to work on it ::sigh::.<br /><br />For mini-micro-spoilers about both books (though really mini when it comes to <i>Love in the Afternoon</i>) go to this interview with Lisa Kleypas that was posted the day after this book came out (Amazon took out the link, so I posted it in the comments section). Thank you to L. ROACH for the post about it; the spoiler for <i>Married by Morning</i> is absolutely great and is a definite must-read if you're left wondering about a certain exchange between Leo and Cat at the end of the book. <br /><br /><b>UPDATE, 6/4/2010:</b><br />Reread and am changing my rating to 3.5 stars; agree with my criticisms and saw all these points as way more of an issue this time. I think the first reading I was somewhat blinded by my excitement to have a new Kleypas book.<br /><br /><b>UPDATE, 5/11/2019:</b><br />Changing it back to 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14957555489971284725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409695079?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bubu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bubu" href="/user/show/44712859-bubu">Bubu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44712859-bubu?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44712859-bubu?shelf=hr">hr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409695079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2558930534909130504"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This is my least favourite of the <i>The Hathaways</i> series, whereas I know a lot of people (including many of my GR friends) loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6264710.Tempt_Me_at_Twilight__The_Hathaways___3_' title='Tempt Me at Twilight (The Hathaways, #3) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tempt Me at Twilight</a>.<br/><br/>I think between Kev and Win's heartbreaking tale and Leo and Kat's almost screwball-y relationship, Poppy and Harry's story remained somewhat bland. It didn't help that the pacing felt uneven, especially after their marriage. Poppy's character seemed inconsistent. I don't know what it was but I simply didn't get her; her feelings for Harry g</span>
  <span id="freeText2558930534909130504" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />This is my least favourite of the <i>The Hathaways</i> series, whereas I know a lot of people (including many of my GR friends) loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6264710.Tempt_Me_at_Twilight__The_Hathaways___3_" title="Tempt Me at Twilight (The Hathaways, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Tempt Me at Twilight</a>.<br /><br />I think between Kev and Win's heartbreaking tale and Leo and Kat's almost screwball-y relationship, Poppy and Harry's story remained somewhat bland. It didn't help that the pacing felt uneven, especially after their marriage. Poppy's character seemed inconsistent. I don't know what it was but I simply didn't get her; her feelings for Harry going back and forth between anger and lust, I didn't see how she'd fall in love with him. Harry is a whole different topic, though. LK's heroes are usually great, either leaning towards darkness (Derek Craven) or sarcasm/irony (St. Vincent), but Harry remained, like Poppy, quite bland. I know he was supposed to be something of an anti-hero, but I missed the edginess that would come along with such a character. All I could see was a manipulator who did things simply because he wanted it that way. <br /><br />This is what happens when I have nothing substential to say about the MC's of a story. I sit here and my brain goes blank. I remember thinking 'I'd rather read Leo's story now.'<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2558930534909130504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_98250069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98250069" />
    <a title="DarienMoya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3069494-darienmoya"><img alt="DarienMoya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536718485p2/3069494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98250069?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DarienMoya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DarienMoya" href="/user/show/3069494-darienmoya">DarienMoya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3069494-darienmoya?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3069494-darienmoya?shelf=fave-books-of-2010">fave-books-of-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3069494-darienmoya?shelf=historical-romances">historical-romances</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98250069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4569858761306720886"> PURE TEMPTATION!!!<br/><br/>The Hathaway's are back and better than ever. This is the third instalment of this quirky, fun and unconventional family,that everywhere they go a scandal follows. This is one is about Poppy the intelligent and beautiful sister who is in London searching for a husband. The hunt is on!<br/><br/>Harry Ruthledge is an enigma in London everyone wants to know who is, where he’s from. Not everyone is privy to that information and that’s how he wants to keep it. He is a famous Hotelier a very </span>
  <span id="freeText4569858761306720886" style="display:none"> PURE TEMPTATION!!!<br /><br />The Hathaway's are back and better than ever. This is the third instalment of this quirky, fun and unconventional family,that everywhere they go a scandal follows. This is one is about Poppy the intelligent and beautiful sister who is in London searching for a husband. The hunt is on!<br /><br />Harry Ruthledge is an enigma in London everyone wants to know who is, where he’s from. Not everyone is privy to that information and that’s how he wants to keep it. He is a famous Hotelier a very rich business man . He keeps everyone at a distance so they wont get too close. So in other words he is a very lonely man, not something he would admit to but its clear for everyone to see. There is only one person who lights his fire and that is Poppy Hathaway. This strong willed independent woman needs a strong man who can appreciate her for who she is, and Harry feels he is just the man. Seems her heart is set on someone else, and Harry will have to use every under handed trick in his book to have her even if she ends up hating him.<br /><br />Poppy knows she scares men away because she tends to chatter away and bring up subjects that are inappropriate, plus she is intelligent. No man wants an intelligent wife its just not done. So Poppy is in love with a Michael Bayning and he is going to offer for her, he just needs to convince his father that she is his perfect match. You see no one wants a Hathaway as a member of the aristocrat because of the scandals and two of her sisters are married to gypsies. So said proposal does not go through and in sweeps Harry who charms a very sad Poppy and leads her into one great big scandal. So in order for them to diminish the scandal a wedding needs to happen pronto. So Poppy is now getting to a man she hardly knows and has no idea if she even likes him. Love matches are for fairytales and marriages of convenience is the norm.<br /><br />This marriage is built on lies and both Harry and Poppy have to come to trust each other and then will they realize that they are perfect together. Lets say that the rest of Poppy’s family did not like the scheming way Harry made Poppy his and they let him know it. Which was hilarious, there’s nothing like having two gypsies threatening your life. The ending was very anticlimactic which I expected more but it doesn’t take anything away from the book. So a woman who has always known love teaches a man who has never had it.<br /><br />I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas" title="Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Kleypas</a> she knows how to write a ruthless bastard, plus the Hathaway’s as a family is pure genius. They are funny and they just don’t give a damn about society’s norm of how they should be. Plus Beatrix is the funniest of the lot, the younger sister who loves animals and treats everyone she encounters as such, I can’t wait for her book. Even if you are not a fan of historical romances you will appreciate this series for what it is, a great and fun filled read and sexy men in breeches.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4569858761306720886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
