<div id="review_132050377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132050377" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132050377?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical romance fans, especially those who like a hero who needs &quot;fixing&quot;</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-lisa-kleypas">author-lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=my-hottie-harem">my-hottie-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=the-hymen-club">the-hymen-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers">keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=covers-to-covet">covers-to-covet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-go-rabid-over">books-i-go-rabid-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132050377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7798737821688480136">It has been a very long time since I picked something up that wasn’t paranormal. But Kleypas’ work makes the transition easy! I’ve only said this about one other author, but whenever I read Kleypas’ books, I don’t feel like I’m reading. Her writing is always so smooth and flawless and every single line flows beautifully. Tempt Me at Twilight is such an enjoyable read! I found myself laughing out loud at some of the lines in here. I need to read the other books!<br/><br/>A large part of the reason why I en</span>
  <span id="freeText7798737821688480136" style="display:none">It has been a very long time since I picked something up that wasn’t paranormal. But Kleypas’ work makes the transition easy! I’ve only said this about one other author, but whenever I read Kleypas’ books, I don’t feel like I’m reading. Her writing is always so smooth and flawless and every single line flows beautifully. Tempt Me at Twilight is such an enjoyable read! I found myself laughing out loud at some of the lines in here. I need to read the other books!<br /><br />A large part of the reason why I enjoyed this book so much was because of Harry. Despite his deception and manipulation, Harry is such an interesting character. From the very beginning, I enjoyed his interactions with Poppy. But after his deception and efforts to make Poppy his wife, I will admit I was a little bit upset to know that he would go through such extremes to have her. It was romantic to know that he would do anything to have her, but I also felt sorry for Michael (even if he was a wuss). I think the reason why Harry was such an appealing character was because he always gets what he wants. And who am I to stop him? His ruthlessness makes him desirable to all females. <br /><br />Poppy was such a great heroine to read about. She’s intelligent, funny, and isn’t afraid to speak her mind. I love the fact that her family is such a large part of her life. She finds comfort in them, but she is also able to stand on her own and still shine. I also adored the fact that she didn’t try to change Harry. Instead, she accepted him for who he was. Not once did she look at his childhood and grimace at his neglected upbringing that makes him so reserved. She accepts it and in turn accepts him, which seems to be a first for Harry. Poppy gives him the chance to be loved for the first time in his lonely life.<br /><br />I also enjoyed the mocking and jabbing between Catherine and Leo. Together, they bicker and criticize each other and it’s downright entertaining to just read about them. I was so stunned to find out about Catherine’s relationship with Harry but in a good way.<br /><br />Tempt Me at Twilight is a great read. The Hathaways series is one that I will keep reading and rave about. LK is truly gifted in what she does.<br /><br />Favourite Quote:<br />The chef looked deeply concerned. “You think there’s a problem with his carrot?”<br />“Watercress, carrot – is everything food to you?” Jake demanded.<br />The chef shrugged. “Oui.”<br />“Well,” Jake said testily, “there is a string of Rutledge’s past mistresses who would undoubtedly testify there is nothing wrong with his carrot.”<br />“Alors, he is a virile man...she is a beautiful woman...why are they not making a salad together?”<br />Pg.203<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7798737821688480136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96181856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96181856" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050338-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474253068p2/3050338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96181856?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/3050338-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=comfort-reads">comfort-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=love-triangle-love-v">love-triangle-love-v</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer96181856&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96181856" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5343483774625167328">Poppy Hathaway just wanted to marry the man she loved and live a nice, peaceful life. Instead, she finds herself chasing a ferret through the Rutledge Hotel, during which she enters a hidden passage, has an intriguing encounter with a mysterious man, and later finds out that he is the illustrious Harry Rutledge, the absentee owner of the hotel. Despite herself, she starts to like the man but she never entertains any kind of romantic notions about him; those she reserves for Michael Bayning.<br/><br/>Howev</span>
  <span id="freeText5343483774625167328" style="display:none">Poppy Hathaway just wanted to marry the man she loved and live a nice, peaceful life. Instead, she finds herself chasing a ferret through the Rutledge Hotel, during which she enters a hidden passage, has an intriguing encounter with a mysterious man, and later finds out that he is the illustrious Harry Rutledge, the absentee owner of the hotel. Despite herself, she starts to like the man but she never entertains any kind of romantic notions about him; those she reserves for Michael Bayning.<br /><br />However, when Michael unceremoniously "dumps" her, she turns to Harry for comfort. And after being found in a compromising position, she eventually agrees to marry him, despite her family's protestations. Poppy goes through with the wedding, however, even after she finds out that Harry was the means by which her break-up with Michael came about.<br /><br />After they're married, Harry and Poppy seem to simply circle around each other, having a few nice moments and having quite a few arguments. Subconsciously, though, the two start to care for each other and tender moments seem to come more frequently.<br /><br />A few months into the marriage, Poppy and Harry finally decide that it's time to consummate the marriage. Upon seeing Poppy in a lot pain, however, Harry pulls out and leaves, going to a tavern to drown his sorrows. While he is gone, Poppy goes to Leo and asks him to escort her to Hampshire. Where she hopes Harry will follow her.<br /><br />Harry does indeed follow and the couple makes up and finally have their way with each other. Poppy convinces him to agree to eleven days in the country, and they come to realize just how much they love each other.<br /><br />When they go back to London, everything is going well, with the exception of Harry and Poppy's fight over her going to see Michael Bayning to try and talk some sense into him so he will stop single-handedly ruining his own life. Upon speaking to Leo about it, Poppy realizes her mistake and then goes to pick up a special present she had made for Harry. Upon coming home that night, Harry, in all his jealousy, demands to know where Poppy was that day. When she tells him and gives him the present (a new watch with his initials on the cover and a special inscription inside), he apologizes and finally admits how much he loves her; later that night she admits the same thing to him.<br /><br />The next day, Harry disappeared.<br /><br />Poppy is convinced he was kidnapped after a certain amount of information came to light, and Jake Valentine, Harry's right-hand man, goes to contact two men that Harry advised him to contact in the event of just such an emergency. Overwhelmed, Poppy takes Leo and they search out Michael Bayning, to see if he had anything to do with the kidnapping. When it is evident that he played no role in it, despite his previous attempt and threats to Harry's life, Poppy's only suspect is Mr. Kinloch, a man who works with guns, whose commission Harry had turned down the day before.<br /><br />Leo, being an architect, goes to Kinloch's house and manages to find a private room. Valentine picks the lock and Harry comes out as Poppy throws herself at him. After giving his statement down at the station, Poppy and Harry go home, where she takes care of him.<br /><br />Three days later, Poppy thinks that it's possible she is pregnant and Harry, overjoyed by the news, takes her into the bedroom in order to make sure that she was.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />The first thing I have to say about this book is this: Move over Cam, it's time to make room for Harry! Seriously, I loved Harry from the beginning, despite his deceptive, mysterious ways. I saw in him a wounded soul and a great capacity to love, if only he could have tapped into that. Harry is witty, intelligent, strong, and extraordinarily loving when he finds someone special enough to care for. Along with all that, though, I loved his darker side, too, and the fact that he could be ruthless if necessary. I finished this book and the moment I closed it, I already thoroughly missed reading about the adorable Harry.<br /><br />Ever since I started reading this series, I've loved all the Hathaway sisters and Poppy has always been one of my favorites (along with Beatrix!), so I was very glad to read her story. Admittedly, there were times when I was utterly frustrated with her (when it looked like she was leaving Harry by going to Hampshire) but I still love her, and I love and appreciate the fact that she was able to open Harry's heart and make him see his capacity for love and that there are people out there who care about him.<br /><br />Since the beginning of the book, I was intrigued by Catherine Marks' continued and vehement dislike of Harry, and I wondered why and what their connection was. Obviously he was someone from her past, but I wondered how she knew him. Imagine my surprise to find that they were siblings! That was certainly an interesting plot twist.<br /><br />As usual, I adore Cam, Kev, and Leo, and I loved seeing them all. I was worried that, with Harry and Poppy living in London that we wouldn't see as much of the Roms and their wives but it was really nice to see them in much of the book. Especially my honey Cam.<br /><br />Beatrix is perpetually charming and I thoroughly look forward to reading her book.<br /><br />As always, Lisa Kleypas does not disappoint and Tempt Me at Twilight was a delightful, beautiful book that I look forward to reading again in the future and continuing the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5343483774625167328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QcIgkidT+JM9Rb3vpSKT4U9BdA3/brG69YSI5vqWlHDKbRCtdT8ohoxNshCw70UkwgSvM9uzCJbVhXY8H4p7EQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rpz4A7eLaYnJNaFSRWCLG7+SCzXn+SLbak32sqvdQanNM8g85ee5nHg9rq1QrV3eMtfQC8Mkm/dKTAhoTsGuyA==')})
  }
